    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<span id="freeTextContainer17971275631817433880">Betsy, Tacy, and Tib are twelve—old enough to do lots of things...even go downtown on their own. There they see their first horseless carriage, discover the joys of the public library, and see a real play at the Opera House. They even find themselves acting in one! Best of all, they help a lonely new friend feel at home in Deep Valley—the most wonderful place in the world </span>
  <span id="freeText17971275631817433880" style="display:none">Betsy, Tacy, and Tib are twelve—old enough to do lots of things...even go downtown on their own. There they see their first horseless carriage, discover the joys of the public library, and see a real play at the Opera House. They even find themselves acting in one! Best of all, they help a lonely new friend feel at home in Deep Valley—the most wonderful place in the world to grow up. Ever since their first publication in the 1940s, the Betsy-Tacy stories have been loved by each generation of young readers.</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/297734020" />
    <a title="Emily" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/343944-emily"><img alt="Emily" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1242156693p2/343944.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/297734020?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily" href="/user/show/343944-emily">Emily</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780690134490" href="/book/show/7905.Betsy_and_Tacy_Go_Downtown">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/343944-emily?shelf=second-childhood">second-childhood</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer297734020" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3237013273506737600">I continue to be amazed at how much I've been enjoying this series on this long-overdue rereading of it. I feel like I know the characters so well, but I found I didn't remember the incidents at all, so it all felt fresh and delightful. My favorite part of this particular book was the Christmas shopping chapter, but I also was very amused at the part when Betsy Tacy and Tib attempt to hypnotize Winona. I'm not particularly a fan of Lois Lenski's illustrations, which I find blocky and wooden (and</span>
  <span id="freeText3237013273506737600" style="display:none">I continue to be amazed at how much I've been enjoying this series on this long-overdue rereading of it. I feel like I know the characters so well, but I found I didn't remember the incidents at all, so it all felt fresh and delightful. My favorite part of this particular book was the Christmas shopping chapter, but I also was very amused at the part when Betsy Tacy and Tib attempt to hypnotize Winona. I'm not particularly a fan of Lois Lenski's illustrations, which I find blocky and wooden (and writing this, I realize that this probably contributed to a false impression on my first reading that the text was correspondingly wooden). However, the picture of the three girls staring at Winona is hilarious.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3237013273506737600" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_6008708" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6008708" />
    <a title="Melody" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/369112-melody"><img alt="Melody" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291050708p2/369112.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6008708?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melody" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melody" href="/user/show/369112-melody">Melody</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/7387710-betsy-and-tacy-go-downtown">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/369112-melody?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6008708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14088672886946818432">9/2012 Six stars. Ninety-six stars. Down Town is my favorite of the first four books and ranks near my favorites in the series entire. I'm prissy about my copy, which is, in fact titled Down Town. None of this namby-pamby <u>Betsy and Tacy Go Downtown</u> stuff. Nope, just Down Town, because like Winona, I like to go in doors marked "Private, Keep Out." <br/><br/>There are so many good stories twining though this book- Mrs. Poppy's, of course. We meet Miss Sparrow here, the librarian who gets so many great lines</span>
  <span id="freeText14088672886946818432" style="display:none">9/2012 Six stars. Ninety-six stars. Down Town is my favorite of the first four books and ranks near my favorites in the series entire. I'm prissy about my copy, which is, in fact titled Down Town. None of this namby-pamby <u>Betsy and Tacy Go Downtown</u> stuff. Nope, just Down Town, because like Winona, I like to go in doors marked "Private, Keep Out." <br /><br />There are so many good stories twining though this book- Mrs. Poppy's, of course. We meet Miss Sparrow here, the librarian who gets so many great lines ("Tom Sawyer- classic- going to be!") and we learn some things about Mrs. Ray's childhood. The Christmas shopping trip! The bobsled, where we first meet Betsy's trick ankle. What fun these people have, and how they love each other.<br /><br />And did you ever notice how in this book Lovelace draws attention to Margaret's thick and lovely eyelashes? <br /><br /><br />12/2009 This is my favorite of the pre-high-school Betsy-Tacy books. Among the BT cognoscenti, whole weeks have been devoted to debating which books in the series are the best. This does sometimes devolve into name-calling and braid-tugging, but generally Down Town ranks near the top.<br /><br />The girls are 12 and they don't quite fit anywhere- not with Julia and Katie who are being walked home from school by boys, and not with Margaret and Freddie who are rioting through the streets shouting. They want to be one or the other but they can't quite decide which. Their parents are becoming more interesting, with backstories of their own- but at the same time less central to the lives of the girls. Betsy is developing some of that tender empathy which will both help her and break her heart in future books. Tacy is settling into her role as champion and cheerleader and Tib... is just like Tib, forever and ever, amen. <br /><br />The lost uncle plotline makes me weep as hard as the Ladies Home Journal story in teeny-tiny writing makes me laugh.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14088672886946818432" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3080315530" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3080315530" />
    <a title="Abigail" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail"><img alt="Abigail" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539121384p2/87835420.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3080315530?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abigail" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abigail" href="/user/show/87835420-abigail">Abigail</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/7387710-betsy-and-tacy-go-downtown">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Readers Who Enjoyed the First Three Betsy-Tacy Books</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Abigail by: </span>
      Many Friends
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=vintage-girls">vintage-girls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/87835420-abigail?shelf=minnesota">minnesota</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3080315530" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16297749575155199354">I think that <u>Betsy and Tacy Go Downtown</u> may be my favorite book yet, in Maud Hart Lovelace's series of children's novels devoted to the adventures of three young girls growing up in late nineteenth and early twentieth-century Minnesota. Now twelve years old, Betsy, Tacy and Tib find their horizons expanding, as they venture into town on their own, see a horseless carriage for the first time, attend a thrilling performance of <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46787.Uncle_Tom_s_Cabin' title='Uncle Tom's Cabin by Harriet Beecher Stowe' rel='nofollow noopener'>Uncle Tom's Cabin</a>
</i> at the Opera House, and (in Betsy's case) discove</span>
  <span id="freeText16297749575155199354" style="display:none">I think that <u>Betsy and Tacy Go Downtown</u> may be my favorite book yet, in Maud Hart Lovelace's series of children's novels devoted to the adventures of three young girls growing up in late nineteenth and early twentieth-century Minnesota. Now twelve years old, Betsy, Tacy and Tib find their horizons expanding, as they venture into town on their own, see a horseless carriage for the first time, attend a thrilling performance of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46787.Uncle_Tom_s_Cabin" title="Uncle Tom's Cabin by Harriet Beecher Stowe" rel="nofollow noopener">Uncle Tom's Cabin</a>
</i> at the Opera House, and (in Betsy's case) discover the joys of the new Carnegie Library. <br /><br />The girls find a new playmate in Winona Root, the sometimes exasperating daughter of Deep Valley's newspaper editor, and a true friend in plump Mrs. Poppy, who gives them a lovely Christmas party. But the most thrilling experience of all comes when they are chosen to participate in a performance of <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/462182.Rip_Van_Winkle" title="Rip Van Winkle by Washington Irving" rel="nofollow noopener">Rip Van Winkle</a>
</i>, and make a surprise discovery with implications for Betsy's family...<br /><br />Like some other reviewers who first read this as an adult, I was able to guess all the developments well in advance. But somehow, the pleasure of "discovery" was in no way diminished - a testament to Lovelace's immense skill as a storyteller. I enjoyed all the adventures chronicled herein, particularly the Christmas "shopping" expedition, and was charmed to follow Betsy's growth as an author. I laughed over her attempted sentimental novel, <i>The Repentance of Lady Clinton</i>, and thrilled to her first success, with the publication of the poem, <i>The Curtain Goes Up</i>. As Lovelace observes at the close of this entertaining and heartwarming story, the curtain is going up on the girls' adolescence, and I, for one, am looking forward to watching it!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16297749575155199354" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_988115890" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/988115890" />
    <a title="Logan Hughes" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15052079-logan-hughes"><img alt="Logan Hughes" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566699500p2/15052079.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/988115890?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Logan Hughes" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Logan Hughes" href="/user/show/15052079-logan-hughes">Logan Hughes</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15052079-logan-hughes?shelf=quaint-youths">quaint-youths</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer988115890" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11834770538540976365">I remembered gap with no book between Betsy's childhood and teenagerhood, but I'd forgotten that this volume takes place in Betsy's twelfth year, and it is appropriately transitional. While Betsy, Tacy, and Tib still get into childlike scrapes and indulge in flights of fancy, they are also more capable and independent, taking trips downtown by themselves. Betsy is as irrepressible as ever and there are certainly charming moments in this book, but I have a few gripes with it (rare for a Betsy boo</span>
  <span id="freeText11834770538540976365" style="display:none">I remembered gap with no book between Betsy's childhood and teenagerhood, but I'd forgotten that this volume takes place in Betsy's twelfth year, and it is appropriately transitional. While Betsy, Tacy, and Tib still get into childlike scrapes and indulge in flights of fancy, they are also more capable and independent, taking trips downtown by themselves. Betsy is as irrepressible as ever and there are certainly charming moments in this book, but I have a few gripes with it (rare for a Betsy book, I know): <br /><br />* <b>Lovingly meticulous description of super-racist media.</b> A major plot point involves getting to go see the play "Uncle Tom's Cabin," which seems to be played by white actors in blackface. The entr'acte entertainment is a blackface band playing minstrel show standards. The girls consider putting on a play themselves with blackface. It's just really creepy all around. If gifting or read-alouding this to a child, you'll have to pair it with a Talk.<br /><br />* <b>Unnecessary, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1934.Little_Women__Little_Women___1_" title="Little Women (Little Women, #1) by Louisa May Alcott" rel="nofollow noopener">Little Women</a>-esque put-down of genre fiction.</b> Betsy's writing at this time centers around mimicry of contemporary "ten-cent novels" like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/588747.Lady_Audley_s_Secret" title="Lady Audley's Secret by Mary Elizabeth Braddon" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady Audley's Secret</a> (which, by the way, I loved). The titles are things like "The Repentence of Lady Clinton" and "Hardly More than a Child." I would LOVE to read these. Unfortunately, she BURNS IT after her mother expresses disappointment that she isn't reading/imitating The Classics. F that! Imitating genre fic is what kids this age do (see the Bronte Sisters' AMAZING juvenilia), PLUS it's a legit way to make money unlike dull imitations of Homer or whatever, PLUS art is subjective, so stuff it, Betsy's Mom. Except I guess the themes are a little adult for a twelve-year-old. <br /><br />* <b>Saccharine long-lost-uncle subplot.</b> Although Maud Hart really did have an estranged theatrical uncle, it's clear that the reunion scene is fake here, because it's just so book-y. It's not terrible, it's just rare for Maud to stray into overwrought, cliche kids' book territory that I don't expect it. <br /><br />That said, there are some classic scenes here, like Betsy/Tacy/Tib attempting to hypnotize Winona, and them inducting Winona into their method of Christmas (window) shopping, and Betsy going to the new library by herself!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11834770538540976365" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2715977941?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebekah Giese Witherspoon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebekah Giese Witherspoon" href="/user/show/25938648-rebekah-giese-witherspoon">Rebekah Giese Witherspoon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780613100113" href="/book/show/3343247-betsy-and-tacy-go-downtown">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2715977941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6444729484297776898">This ode to books and love letter to libraries opens with a crisis. Betsy has read all of the books in her house. What is an aspiring writer to do? She borrows some scandalous dime novels and Tacy follows Betsy’s example, with disastrous results (a wink and a smile to fellow fans of Victorian sensation novels):<br/><br/><i>“You remember,” she said, “Rena loaned me <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/588747.Lady_Audley_s_Secret' title='Lady Audley's Secret by Mary Elizabeth Braddon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Lady Audley's Secret</a>. Well, Papa found it.” Tacy began to sob. “Papa said he was amazed and astounded. He said he thought he had brought us up to </i></span>
  <span id="freeText6444729484297776898" style="display:none">This ode to books and love letter to libraries opens with a crisis. Betsy has read all of the books in her house. What is an aspiring writer to do? She borrows some scandalous dime novels and Tacy follows Betsy’s example, with disastrous results (a wink and a smile to fellow fans of Victorian sensation novels):<br /><br /><i>“You remember,” she said, “Rena loaned me <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/588747.Lady_Audley_s_Secret" title="Lady Audley's Secret by Mary Elizabeth Braddon" rel="nofollow noopener">Lady Audley's Secret</a>. Well, Papa found it.” Tacy began to sob. “Papa said he was amazed and astounded. He said he thought he had brought us up to appreciate good literature. He said there was a set of Dickens in the house, and Shakespeare, and Father Finn, and how did a child of his happen to be reading trash?”<br /><br />“Trash!” cried Betsy. “I’m trying to write books just like it.”</i><br /><br />The very first library in town finally opens and saves Betsy’s literary life.<br /><br /><i>She tried to act as though it were nothing to go to the library alone. But her happiness betrayed her. Her smile could not be restrained, and it spread from her tightly pressed mouth, to her round cheeks, almost to the hair ribbons tied in perky bows over her ears…. She seated herself in the chair nearest the fire, piled the books beside her and opened <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/44039569.Tanglewood_Tales" title="Tanglewood Tales by Nathaniel Hawthorne" rel="nofollow noopener">Tanglewood Tales</a>. But she did not start to read at once. Before she began she smiled at the fire, she smiled at her books, she smiled broadly all around the room. Betsy…opened her book and forgot the world again.</i><br /><br />The literary references throughout are charming. There’s even a reference to “a new song called The Rosary”, of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8159356.The_Rosary" title="The Rosary by Florence Louisa Barclay" rel="nofollow noopener">The Rosary</a> fame. Betsy’s passion for books of all sorts makes her a kindred spirit indeed.<br /><br />My only disappointment in this book is the unexplained absence of their friend Naifi and the lovely Syrian community, all of whom we met in the previous book. Such a lovely series!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6444729484297776898" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3222109433" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3222109433" />
    <a title="Bev" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5082359-bev"><img alt="Bev" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1374365942p2/5082359.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3222109433?book_show_action=true">Mar 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bev" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bev" href="/user/show/5082359-bev">Bev</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/52197606-betsy-and-tacy-go-downtown">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=mount-tbr-2020">mount-tbr-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=childrens">childrens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5082359-bev?shelf=classic-lit">classic-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3222109433" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7754734342460125340">I loved this book when I was growing up and read it many, many times. I always wanted to write stories like Betsy did.<br/><br/>3/10/20: While sorting through storage bins in the garage, I came across this childhood favorite. It's the only book in the Betsy and Tacy series I ever read and as far I'm concerned that's fine with me. It was an absolute perfect book for this born reader and writer-wannabe. I loved Betsy. I knew exactly how she felt making her first trip to the town's brand new Carnegie library</span>
  <span id="freeText7754734342460125340" style="display:none">I loved this book when I was growing up and read it many, many times. I always wanted to write stories like Betsy did.<br /><br />3/10/20: While sorting through storage bins in the garage, I came across this childhood favorite. It's the only book in the Betsy and Tacy series I ever read and as far I'm concerned that's fine with me. It was an absolute perfect book for this born reader and writer-wannabe. I loved Betsy. I knew exactly how she felt making her first trip to the town's brand new Carnegie library. I still remember my mom taking me to ours and how excited I was to get my first library card (with a metal piece in it and the ka-chunk noise the machine made when the card was used to check out books). I, too, had little notebooks in which I wrote miniature stories. For me, it was mysteries featuring the "Crime Club"--a group of friends not too unlike Trixie Belden and her Bob Whites. Unlike Betsy, I did not shove them in the fire and move on to writing classic-like stories. But I have no idea what happened to those little notebooks with "The Diamond Bracelet Mystery" and others in them...<br /><br />There are so many things to like about this book. The friendship between Betsy and Tacy and Tib. The way they try to hypnotize Winona Root into taking them to the theater and the friendship that develops thereafter. Winona's surprise for Betsy and her poem. Tib's ride in the town's first-ever horseless carriage. Mrs. Poppy, her quest to belong in her new town, and the heart-warming surprise she makes happen for Betsy and her family. The girls' Christmas shopping trip. The Christmas traditions of Betsy's family. And--Betsy's love of books and story-telling. A truly heart-warming book that was just as much fun to read as an adult as it was when I was young. <br /><br />First posted on my blog <a href="https://myreadersblock.blogspot.com/2020/03/betsy-tacy-go-downtown.html" rel="nofollow noopener">My Reader's Block</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="7754734342460125340" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_8082129" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8082129" />
    <a title="Carmen Maloy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/563625-carmen-maloy"><img alt="Carmen Maloy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1195667618p2/563625.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/8082129?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carmen Maloy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carmen Maloy" href="/user/show/563625-carmen-maloy">Carmen Maloy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Everyone</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8082129" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5709085187204766656">This is the last of the "younger" Betsy books, taking us to turn of the century Minnesota, horse-less carriages, and many wonderful new friends. BTGD introduces us to Winona Root, Mrs. Poppy, and some of the places and items we will know and love in the "high school" books. A wonderful look at the transition into adolecense. We also read about the tradition of the annual christmas shopping trip that Betsy and Tacy take together. On a personal note, this is a tradition that my sisters and I do ev</span>
  <span id="freeText5709085187204766656" style="display:none">This is the last of the "younger" Betsy books, taking us to turn of the century Minnesota, horse-less carriages, and many wonderful new friends. BTGD introduces us to Winona Root, Mrs. Poppy, and some of the places and items we will know and love in the "high school" books. A wonderful look at the transition into adolecense. We also read about the tradition of the annual christmas shopping trip that Betsy and Tacy take together. On a personal note, this is a tradition that my sisters and I do every year in honor of the books and it's a blast. <br /><br />The Betsy-Tacy books were highly autobiographical and Lovelace perfectly captures the innocence and magic of childhood. If you read this book and love it, please read the series. It will be books that you will never forget as long as you live. I also recommend the "Betsy-Tacy Companion" which is an amazing book that disects each book and compares it to it's real-life counterparts, including pictures of the "real" Betsy, Tacy, Tib and all the gang. <br /><br />I had the pleasure of visiting "Deep Valley" (aka Mankato, Minnesota) for a Betsy-Tacy convention back in 1996. It was incredible to step back in time and enter Betsy's world. We toured the city and I was actually able to step foot in "Tacy's" bedroom and sit on the famous bench at the top of the big hill. It was truly a life-altering experience. I have to thank my sister, Julie for introducting these books to me and changing my life. <br /><br />It's obvious how much these books mean to me. My first born child was named Tacy Kelly Maloy. Please read and enjoy. They are a treasure! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5709085187204766656" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hope" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hope" href="/user/show/13246091-hope">Hope</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13246091-hope?shelf=childrens-lit">childrens-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13246091-hope?shelf=light-reading">light-reading</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1142225531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16539034677709807751">The story is about two little girls growing up in Minnesota at the turn of the century, a time when cars and telephones were new and exciting inventions. The book opens with references to Lady Audley’s Secret and contains many delightful allusions to books throughout its pages.<br/><br/>Twelve year old Betsy is an aspiring writer. Unfortunately she’s been influenced by sensational and melodramatic novels and is writing stories with similar themes (“Lady Gwendolyn’s Sin”). Betsy’s mother and father handle </span>
  <span id="freeText16539034677709807751" style="display:none">The story is about two little girls growing up in Minnesota at the turn of the century, a time when cars and telephones were new and exciting inventions. The book opens with references to Lady Audley’s Secret and contains many delightful allusions to books throughout its pages.<br /><br />Twelve year old Betsy is an aspiring writer. Unfortunately she’s been influenced by sensational and melodramatic novels and is writing stories with similar themes (“Lady Gwendolyn’s Sin”). Betsy’s mother and father handle this problem with gentleness and sensitivity. Instead of condemning her, her father gives her a library card and 15 cents for lunch so that she can spend all day Saturday in town, reading the classics. Her trips to town open up a new world to her.<br /><br />Betsy and Tacy Go Downtown is a book about simple pleasures and great kindnesses. With its references to classic books, it’s good writing, and it’s pleasant tone, I (who am 52 years old) found it hard to put down. </span>
  <a data-text-id="16539034677709807751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/83445-lisa-vegan?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8077310" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7729207865072150950">Once again, this fourth book in the Betsy-Tacy series is well written and full of emotionally lovely moments. As an adult reading it for the first time, I saw the story lines coming from a million miles away but I thoroughly enjoyed them anyway. Some of the more old-fashioned stuff such as the furs and performance of the play Uncle Tom’s Cabin (the latter of which I’m sure was ahead for its time) rubbed me slightly the wrong way, and I’d have loved to hear more about the new library and Betsy’s </span>
  <span id="freeText7729207865072150950" style="display:none">Once again, this fourth book in the Betsy-Tacy series is well written and full of emotionally lovely moments. As an adult reading it for the first time, I saw the story lines coming from a million miles away but I thoroughly enjoyed them anyway. Some of the more old-fashioned stuff such as the furs and performance of the play Uncle Tom’s Cabin (the latter of which I’m sure was ahead for its time) rubbed me slightly the wrong way, and I’d have loved to hear more about the new library and Betsy’s library books, but I loved the parts about Mrs. Poppy and, as usual, everything about the friendships of the girls. These books are a real pleasure. The next two: Heaven to Betsy and Betsy in Spite of Herself, which I’ll read next, are the only two I read when I was young, at least I’m reasonably sure that I did; I’m eager to find out what I remember from them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7729207865072150950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2551623393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6657627021213599477">These books are excellent. <br/><br/>Yes. They are dated. There are references to theatrical practices that have thankfully gone away.<br/><br/><br/>However, these books are so matter-of-fact to the heart of how girls grow up. Stripped of technology and peer pressure and too-busy-ness of the present day, this is how it is to be twelve.<br/><br/><br/>My daughter would adore the library day (me too) that Betsy has. It's magic.<br/><br/><br/>Just read them and judge for yourself.<br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_89448089" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/89448089" />
    <a title="Mel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/528350-mel"><img alt="Mel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1579480717p2/528350.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/89448089?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mel" href="/user/show/528350-mel">Mel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer89448089" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2183413851023881290">Once again, Betsy and Tacy exceeded expectations!<br/><br/>In what I would call the final installment of the “childhood” portion of this series, “Betsy and Tacy Go Downtown” – the girls are now 12 years old and, according to them, “all grown up.”<br/><br/>Their escapades continue – riding in a horseless carriage (a car!), beguiling their new friend, Winona, going to the theatre, befriending an unexpected companion, acting on stage and discovering a long, lost relative!<br/><br/>So many things to adore in this book! For those</span>
  <span id="freeText2183413851023881290" style="display:none">Once again, Betsy and Tacy exceeded expectations!<br /><br />In what I would call the final installment of the “childhood” portion of this series, “Betsy and Tacy Go Downtown” – the girls are now 12 years old and, according to them, “all grown up.”<br /><br />Their escapades continue – riding in a horseless carriage (a car!), beguiling their new friend, Winona, going to the theatre, befriending an unexpected companion, acting on stage and discovering a long, lost relative!<br /><br />So many things to adore in this book! For those who love the theatre (a paramount requirement in our family!) there are several chapters on that theme. Do you enjoy Christmas traditions? A chapter on that. A love of the library and all things literary? Betsy is euphoric when she is allowed to go the library ALONE every other Saturday. She also blossoms into a poet and writer. The relationship between Mrs. Poppy and Betsy is one of particular importance. It shows how mercy and compassion can transcend the difference between age, cultural upbringing and social status. A sweet, sweet book. If you read only one Betsy book this is the one to read.<br /><br />My daughter’s favorite part: “…acting on stage! I want to do that when I grow up!” She is a closet theatre geek – she’s been going to theatre since she was 4. Her first musical, Annie. I hope she will audition some day!<br /><br />Our mother/daughter book group meets tomorrow night for our discussion. This is the final Betsy Tacy book for us. We will be picking a new series/author/theme for March.<br /><br />Any good ideas/recommendations?? And something short? March is Spring Break!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2183413851023881290" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780690134506" href="/book/show/3343246-betsy-and-tacy-go-downtown">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7098916-elizabeth?shelf=beautiful-girlhood">beautiful-girlhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7098916-elizabeth?shelf=children-s">children-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7098916-elizabeth?shelf=classics">classics</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655714854" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15544890324710604015">I needed to visit downtown Deep Valley last night and take that first horseless carriage ride with the lovable Poppys and Tib. Also, I just crack up when the trio try to hypnotize Winona to try to get her to take them to see Uncle Tom's Cabin. Then to find out that she wanted to take them all along...so sweet. I love when they go to the oprea house and they are full of all that excitement of uninhibited childhood.<br/><br/>This is my favorite in the series. I love Betsy's first trip to the new library whe</span>
  <span id="freeText15544890324710604015" style="display:none">I needed to visit downtown Deep Valley last night and take that first horseless carriage ride with the lovable Poppys and Tib. Also, I just crack up when the trio try to hypnotize Winona to try to get her to take them to see Uncle Tom's Cabin. Then to find out that she wanted to take them all along...so sweet. I love when they go to the oprea house and they are full of all that excitement of uninhibited childhood.<br /><br />This is my favorite in the series. I love Betsy's first trip to the new library where she sits in front of the cozy fire. I love the wisdom from her parents about how she should read classic books to become a good writer. I love all the snow scenes and the bobsled party. Love Mrs. Poppy. I like the age of the girls in this one; they are 12 so though they play with dolls, they only do so when sick. They are still little girls but they are growing up. I love their friendships and how they encourage each other....sending Betsy's story off to Lady's Home Journal. <br /><br />Ohh and I do love the Christmas in this one and how the entire Ray family is excited for little Margaret to get her little doll that says "mama" if it's squeezed.<br /><br />Sigh....I wish I could jump into this book and be their friend.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1222844768?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie" href="/user/show/5885029-bonnie">Bonnie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780690134506" href="/book/show/3343246-betsy-and-tacy-go-downtown">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1222844768" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1947765702776223135">I've never read a Betsy-Tacy book, though I have several friends who are fans. And normally, OCD me would never start a series without starting at #1 but this book, the fourth in the series, is one of my Literary Map of the United States books. I enjoyed it so much that I almost stopped reading very early on, in order to go and get the first three books from the library before continuing. But I have a lot of reading goals this year, so I opted to just continue with book four and try and get back</span>
  <span id="freeText1947765702776223135" style="display:none">I've never read a Betsy-Tacy book, though I have several friends who are fans. And normally, OCD me would never start a series without starting at #1 but this book, the fourth in the series, is one of my Literary Map of the United States books. I enjoyed it so much that I almost stopped reading very early on, in order to go and get the first three books from the library before continuing. But I have a lot of reading goals this year, so I opted to just continue with book four and try and get back to the rest of the series "someday". Deep Valley is based on Mankato, Minnesota, a town I'm familiar with due to the Little House series. The book covers several adventures of 12yo Betsy and her best friends Tacy and Tib (which makes me wonder why the series isn't the Betsy-Tacy-Tib series?), mainly focused around the town's Opera House and a few plays that come through town. It was a delightful young readers book with lots of incidents that made me smile. As far as the Literary Map of the U.S. goes, I thought the descriptions of the town, the people, and events, were all very well done and really put me there in small town Minnesota.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1947765702776223135" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5065829645470445310">This was my favorite of the Betsy-Tacy books growing up. I loved the introduction of technology (the horseless carriage or automobile) to small town Minnesota, the long lost brother plot line, and that Betsy was developing her passion for writing.   <span id="freeText5065829645470445310" style="display:none">This was my favorite of the Betsy-Tacy books growing up. I loved the introduction of technology (the horseless carriage or automobile) to small town Minnesota, the long lost brother plot line, and that Betsy was developing her passion for writing. All things were achievable and all endings were happy in early 1900s Deep Valley (Mankato) Minnesota. <br />Upon this most recent reread, I wasn't quite as fascinated my the idea of a horseless carriage and the long lost brother plot line was not as believable. Yet, out of the four stories about Betsy's (Maud's) childhood, this one remains the quintessential story of childhood. Old enough for a little independence and young enough for the simplicities of being a kid.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1535221719739422635">I saw one person's comment that the world of Betsy-Tacy probably doesn't exist in America, but I disagree. I can remember being old enough to go downtown without parents. Sharing it with a best friend or two made it even better. What makes Lovelace's books so great is that it was, and in a few special places still is, life in small-town America.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('2Hh3kO2Wf3T2nv+KGCC2KqwkSGw1SkzMuGSiPPJkGquruxWief6u5pogPVL0gV9PsPnrsesQvWOlf8I3eXKLnA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7355451406538093714">Maud Hart Lovelace was born on April 25, 1892, in Mankato, Minnesota. She was the middle of three children born to Thomas and Stella (Palmer) Hart. Her sister, Kathleen, was three years older, and her other sister, Helen, was six years younger. “That dear family" was the model for the fictional Ray family.<br/><br/>Maud’s birthplace was a small house on a hilly residential street several blocks above Mankat</span>
  <span id="freeText7355451406538093714" style="display:none">Maud Hart Lovelace was born on April 25, 1892, in Mankato, Minnesota. She was the middle of three children born to Thomas and Stella (Palmer) Hart. Her sister, Kathleen, was three years older, and her other sister, Helen, was six years younger. “That dear family" was the model for the fictional Ray family.<br /><br />Maud’s birthplace was a small house on a hilly residential street several blocks above Mankato’s center business district. The street, Center Street, dead-ended at one of the town’s many hills. When Maud was a few months old, the Hart family moved two blocks up the street to 333 Center. <br /><br />Shortly before Maud’s fifth birthday a “large merry Irish family" moved into the house directly across the street. Among its many children was a girl Maud’s age, Frances, nicknamed Bick, who was to be Maud’s best friend and the model for Tacy Kelly. <br /><br />Tib’s character was based on another playmate, Marjorie (Midge) Gerlach, who lived nearby in a large house designed by her architect father. Maud, Bick, and Midge became lifelong friends. Maud once stated that the three couldn’t have been closer if they’d been sisters.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7355451406538093714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
